  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_31eef369-588e-4031-8b39-14de39cffa50'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText3399932784030236698" style="display:none"><b>Two women on either side of the Silver and Red divide tell the stories no one else knows.</b><br /><br /><i>Discover the truth of Norta’s bloody past in these two revealing prequels to #1 </i>NEW YORK TIMES<i> bestseller </i>RED QUEEN.<br /><br /><b>Queen Song</b><br /><br />Queen Coriane, first wife of King Tiberias, keeps a secret diary—how else can she ensure that no one at the palace will use her thoughts against her? Coriane recounts her heady courtship with the crown prince, the birth of a new prince, Cal, and the potentially deadly challenges that lie ahead for her in royal life.<br /><br /><b>Steel Scars</b><br /><br />Captain Farley was raised to be strong, but being tasked with planting the seeds of rebellion in Norta is a tougher job than expected. As she travels the land recruiting black market traders, smugglers, and extremists for her first attempt at an attack on the capital, she stumbles upon a connection that may prove to be the key to the entire operation—Mare Barrow.<br /><br />Plus a <b>Glass Sword</b> sneak peek!<br /><br />An exclusive excerpt of the hotly anticipated second book in the Red Queen series, <i>Glass Sword</i>, transports readers to the world of Silver tyranny, a Red dawn rising, and one girl’s resolve to break down the system that will hold her back no longer.</span>

<div id="review_2447449282" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2447449282" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2447449282?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2447449282" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17808408182127556559"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566623615i/28042841._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i> There is nothing so terrible as a story untold.</i>**</blockquote> **There is nothing so terrible as <b>
  <i>this</i>
</b> story being told. <br/><br/>So, we get the <b>
  <i>absolutely essential</i>
</b> novellas chronicling the lives of<b>
  <i> incredible women</i>
</b> who play <b>
  <i>pivotal roles</i>
</b> in the Red Queen series.<br/><br/>Thus with heartfelt cheer and warmest wishes, Victoria Aveyard graces her audience with yet another <b>
  <u>completely useless and half-assed book.</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>“There is no greater pain or punishment then memory.” </i>
</blockquote> <b>I honestly laughed</b> when I first read th</span>
  <span id="freeText17808408182127556559" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566623615i/28042841._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i> There is nothing so terrible as a story untold.</i>**</blockquote> **There is nothing so terrible as <b>
  <i>this</i>
</b> story being told. <br><br>So, we get the <b>
  <i>absolutely essential</i>
</b> novellas chronicling the lives of<b>
  <i> incredible women</i>
</b> who play <b>
  <i>pivotal roles</i>
</b> in the Red Queen series.<br><br>Thus with heartfelt cheer and warmest wishes, Victoria Aveyard graces her audience with yet another <b>
  <u>completely useless and half-assed book.</u>
</b><blockquote>
  <i>“There is no greater pain or punishment then memory.” </i>
</blockquote> <b>I honestly laughed</b> when I first read that quote but now...after making my way through these novellas. I get it.<b> Truer words, never spoken.</b><br><br><b>
  <u>Queen Song</u>
</b><br><br>Right off the bat, shouldn't the title be<b> Queen's Song? </b><br><br>Anyway, it took me <b>roughly half the book</b> to figure out who this Coriane was - turns out she's Prince Cal's mom - who spends the entire book complaining about Elara (Prince Maven's mom).<br><br>Once I figured out who was who...I knew that this was not going to end well. Why? Cause we were already told the entire plot of this one in the original novels.<br><br>Let me repeat that.<br><br><b>
  <u>We already know what happened.</u>
</b><br><br>So...this begs the question - <b>why write a novella? </b>Because some stories are <s>just meant to be told</s> too good to pass up on a money grab.<br><br>After all, these are the two women responsible Mare's <b>greatest life dilemma </b>- does she go with good-guy-hottie (Coriane's brat) or bad-guy-hottie (Elara's spawn).<i> Oh the decisions!</i><br><br>Anyway - Coriane wins the King's heart, marries him, is driven insane by Elara and then kills herself. <b>What. A. Shocker.</b><br><br>As an aside, I can't be the only one<b> seeing the flaw </b>with the way the royalty choose their spouses. <br><br>They set up a huge tournament and whichever minor nobility manages to kill their competition gets to marry the king. So, the goal is to find the<b> strongest, cruelest and bloodthirstiest woman..<i>.then hand her the crown. </i></b><br><br>Really? <br><br>And then everyone gets so shocked when someone murders the king. <b>Wake up people.</b><br><br><b>
  <u>Steel Scars</u>
</b><br><br>Right off the<b> [redacted], </b>Farley doesn't get <b>[redacted] </b>or <b>[redacted] </b>by steel. So, I don't know where this title thought it was <b> [redacted].</b><br><br>In fact, so much of this novella was<b> [redacted]</b> that I literally wanted to <b>[redacted] [redacted] [redacted]</b> up its<b> [redacted]. </b><br><br>Anyway, this one follows Captain Farley - the only captain who managed to touch up her bright red hair on the battle field to keep away those pesky roots. <b>Truly an inspiration.</b><br><br>For such an <b>exciting-sounding plot</b> ("recruiting black market traders, smugglers, and extremists"), Victoria Aveyard sure knows how to <b>tone it down. </b><br><br>The<b> most intriguing mystery</b> was <b>
  <i>the accent.</i>
</b> <br><br>Farley has this <b>over-the-top-posh British accent</b> throughout the audiobooks and yet <b>literally everyone else</b> has a very standard American accents. <i>Could she be a spy?</i><br><br>Even if she's from a different area of the country (somewhere where they mysteriously have British accents) - you'd think there would be <b>at least one person </b>with a similar accent.<i> Is she a redcoat traitor?</i><br><br>Anyway, after finishing this novel, I'm disappointed to note that there are no new developments on <b>
  <i> Accent Watch: Farley Edition </i>
</b> but I'm fully confident that Aveyard is planning a grand reveal in War Storm that will settle all our anxieties.<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>I just looked it up and this one was read by Andi Arndt, Jayne Entwistle, and Amanda Dolan. I literally couldn't tell that there was more than one reader. Someone wasted a lot of money on that audio.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_1364103648" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1364103648" />
    <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli"><img alt="Pearl Angeli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588420465p2/31514572.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1364103648?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=owned-physical-copy">owned-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=young-adult-fantasy">young-adult-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1364103648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer478503000409027715"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25944381.Cruel_Crown__Red_Queen___0_1__0_2_' title='Cruel Crown (Red Queen, #0.1-#0.2) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cruel Crown</a> consists of two novellas, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25005214.Queen_Song__Red_Queen___0_1_' title='Queen Song (Red Queen, #0.1) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Queen Song</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25362018.Steel_Scars__Red_Queen___0_2_' title='Steel Scars (Red Queen, #0.2) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Steel Scars</a>. While I loved Queen Song, Steel Cars disappointed me in an epic level. I'm still glad I was able to experience them, though-- Queen Song, especially, because it was simply amazing. :)<br/><br/>My reviews for both novellas:<br/><br/> <u><b>QUEEN SONG</b> </u><br/><br/><blockquote>
<i><b>"There is nothing so terrible as a story untold."</b></i> </blockquote><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25005214.Queen_Song__Red_Queen___0_1_' title='Queen Song (Red Queen, #0.1) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Queen Song</a> is one of the novellas of <b>Red Queen</b> series. Here, we are told about the backstory of <b>Queen Coriane</b>, the mother of <b>Prince Cal</b> from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_' title='Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red Queen</a>. Coriane</span>
  <span id="freeText478503000409027715" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25944381.Cruel_Crown__Red_Queen___0_1__0_2_" title="Cruel Crown (Red Queen, #0.1-#0.2) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Crown</a> consists of two novellas, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25005214.Queen_Song__Red_Queen___0_1_" title="Queen Song (Red Queen, #0.1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Queen Song</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25362018.Steel_Scars__Red_Queen___0_2_" title="Steel Scars (Red Queen, #0.2) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Steel Scars</a>. While I loved Queen Song, Steel Cars disappointed me in an epic level. I'm still glad I was able to experience them, though-- Queen Song, especially, because it was simply amazing. :)<br><br>My reviews for both novellas:<br><br> <u><b>QUEEN SONG</b> </u><br><br><blockquote>
<i><b>"There is nothing so terrible as a story untold."</b></i> </blockquote><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25005214.Queen_Song__Red_Queen___0_1_" title="Queen Song (Red Queen, #0.1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Queen Song</a> is one of the novellas of <b>Red Queen</b> series. Here, we are told about the backstory of <b>Queen Coriane</b>, the mother of <b>Prince Cal</b> from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>. Coriane belongs to the Silver blood, under the <i>House Jacos</i>-- a not-so-well-endowed clan compared to other Silver bloods. She writes her life events in a dairy and conveys her emotions there. Her ordinary life changed when <b>Prince Tibe</b>, heir to the <i>court of Norta</i>, fell in love with her and asked her hand for marriage, which of course, became the reason why the traditional <i>Queenstrial</i> was never realized. This led to conflicts and certain intrigues that tested Coriane's strength and belief while carrying her crown as a Queen.<br><br>It's Victoria Aveyard's flawless and breathtaking writing style that made me embrace this novella. Once again I was amazed by how she was able to bring this story in an epic level. There were no action scenes here but all the events were simply engaging. I loved how the simple plotline surprisingly became extraordinarily beautiful in the end.<br><br>The <b>romance</b> between Coriane and Tibe was sweet and raw, heartbreaking at times. There was also a good pacing here and the Silver blood's powers were drawn neatly.<br><br>Perhaps Coriane's <b>character development</b> was the one that's lacking here. She came out fragile and weak in the beginning but she was starting to get tough in the near-end. Unfortunately, she went back to being weak again in the end, surrendering to her fate and accepting her vulnerability that she couldn't do anything to save herself and the people she cared about.<br><br>All in all, this novella is totally compelling despite some minor flaws. It's nice to know Coriane's story after she was mysteriously mentioned in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>. It was written in a poignant yet beautiful prose, something that holds you together to read it. When it comes to the ending, it was a bit hazy and mind-boggling, thus leaving us with a big question: <b>WHO DID IT?</b><br><br>Rating:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445994440i/16731146.jpg" width="200" height="45" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><u><b>STEEL SCARS</b> </u><br><br>I thought by reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25362018.Steel_Scars__Red_Queen___0_2_" title="Steel Scars (Red Queen, #0.2) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Steel Scars</a> I would be in for a badass story. Nope.<br><br>It was the most boring novella I've read for a YA fantasy book. <b>Farley's</b> character is dull and boring. The only one that made this novella quite interesting is <b>Shade Barrow</b>, but everything is disappointing.<br><br>I don't know if I'm the only one who has this problem, but the narrative reports by the <i>Scarlet Guard</i> are too difficult to comprehend. I don't even know what those are all about. They are too technical!<br><br>I expected some revelations and actions scenes. There are NONE. :(<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454222108ra/17932020.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Rating:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1447324535i/16987052.jpg" width="200" height="45" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>CRUEL CROWN OVERALL RATING:</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446078794i/16744105.jpg" width="200" height="45" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><p>
  <a href="https://bibliopearl.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446199662i/16763926._SX540_.jpg" alt="Pearl's Book Journey (1)" width="380" height="190" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</p><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445993261i/16730770.jpg" width="200" height="120" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>-------------------------------------------------------<br><br><b>THE EXCITEMENT!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439602234ra/15859735.gif" width="250" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1593636934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7226668258918750070">A compilation of two short novellas, 'Cruel Crown' provides a glimpse into the past, as well as a bit more insight into the story's present. The first novella tells the story of the young Coriane and Tiberias. The second novella focuses on the life of Farley as she works to lead an uprising, eventually finding a leader in Mare.<br/><br/>I absolutely loved hearing Coraline's story. This novella made me see King Tiberias as vulnerable and human. They did truly love one another and her life was ended too ear</span>
  <span id="freeText7226668258918750070" style="display:none">A compilation of two short novellas, 'Cruel Crown' provides a glimpse into the past, as well as a bit more insight into the story's present. The first novella tells the story of the young Coriane and Tiberias. The second novella focuses on the life of Farley as she works to lead an uprising, eventually finding a leader in Mare.<br /><br />I absolutely loved hearing Coraline's story. This novella made me see King Tiberias as vulnerable and human. They did truly love one another and her life was ended too early.<br /><br /> I appreciated the additional information and the history that was provided in the first part. I absolutely relished the love story between Coraline's and Tiberias. Unfortunately, the first novella was over too quickly for my liking. Then it was nothing but gloom and doom.<br /><br />After Tiberias and Coraline's story ends, we fast forward several years and change to Farley's POV. From that point forward, the story failed to hold much appeal for me. It was like listening to wartime radio transmissions, separated by large amounts of time and growing progressively more depressing. Here and there I heard something that was interesting. However, as a whole, the second half of 'Cruel Crown' fell flat for me.<br /><br />I'm torn down the middle with this one. I would give it 4-stars for the first novella, but only 2-stars for the second one. Since I can't do that, I'm going with a 3-star rating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7226668258918750070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1759313641" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1759313641" />
    <a title="Alaina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50620706-alaina"><img alt="Alaina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451325817p2/50620706.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1759313641?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alaina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alaina" href="/user/show/50620706-alaina">Alaina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=novellas">novellas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50620706-alaina?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1759313641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6575056888587748581"><b>first time audio. third time reading.</b><br/><br/><i>Cruel Crown</i> is one of those novellas that makes me jealous. Why? Well, I got to meet Cal's mom and now I wish I got more. After her short ass story, well.. I wanted more. She is definitely one of those characters that I wanted to know more about. Ugh, especially since she died from the evil selfish queen bitch.<br/><br/>Then there's Farley.. and eh. She's an okay character. I'm glad I got to see a different side of her and her dad. I'm also glad to see her relationship</span>
  <span id="freeText6575056888587748581" style="display:none"><b>first time audio. third time reading.</b><br /><br /><i>Cruel Crown</i> is one of those novellas that makes me jealous. Why? Well, I got to meet Cal's mom and now I wish I got more. After her short ass story, well.. I wanted more. She is definitely one of those characters that I wanted to know more about. Ugh, especially since she died from the evil selfish queen bitch.<br /><br />Then there's Farley.. and eh. She's an okay character. I'm glad I got to see a different side of her and her dad. I'm also glad to see her relationship with Shade on a deeper level. Watching that romance blossom was sweet. The sexual tension was intense and I could see how they liked each other.<br /><br />Overall, the book was way too short. I wanted more of Cal's mom and her journals. Less of Farley really.<br />____________________________________________________________<br />Second time read and first time review.<br /><br />I really need to stop slacking on reviews for books that I've already read! Okay, so, <i>Cruel Crown</i> has two novellas within it: Queen's Song and Steel Scars. In these books you will get to know Cal's mother and more about Farley and Shade's relationship. They were both super quick and cute reads. <br /><br /><b>Queen's Song:</b><br />Now this book made me love Coriane so much! She was such a sweet and innocent girl who fell in love with a guy. Prince Tiberias and her had such a cute friendship before they got married. I loved how he gave her a fire within herself. Cori knew that Elara was up to something, and oh yes - you meet that little twat in this book too. Elara is vicious and such a savage. Usually I like this in a character but I did not like how she used her powers against Coriane until the day she died. I felt so bad for her because this type of bullying was the extreme. <br /><br />The things that Cori went through were so sad. The amount of babies she lost or the deaths she noted in her little secret diary were too much. She was falling into a deep and dark depression with the help of someone evil inside her head. I was hoping that she would fight more but I already knew she was going to die from <i>Red Queen</i>.<br /><br />After reading this book, well.. I really did wish I actually got to meet her in the first book, <i>Red Queen</i>. To see her being a Queen and a mother to Cal would've been amazing. I'm sad that I didn't get to meet her then but I am happy I got to meet her in this book. Even if it was way too short.<br /><br /><b>Steel Scars:</b><br />Captain Farley wasn't, and still isn't, one of my favorite characters in the <i>Red Queen</i> series. I've wanted to like her so many times.. but it just hasn't happened. I did, however, really enjoy her cute ass friendship/relationship with Shade. I'm really glad I got to know more about him before his untimely death. <br /><br />Seeing her POV when she met Mare, Shade's sister, was interesting but I mostly cared about Shade protecting his sister. He knew that something was up with the army and you could see the wheels turning in his brain trying to come with a plan to save himself and Mare. I also really liked how Farley didn't hesitate to help him either. They both knew that what happened to Mare during the Queenstrial was going to be bigger and more important than anyone expected.<br /><br />Overall, I'm really glad that I got to know more about Shade and Coriane. I miss them already and now I can't wait to dive into <i>War Storm</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6575056888587748581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Luke Taylor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30710594-luke-taylor"><img alt="Luke Taylor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522269800p2/30710594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1469185989?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luke Taylor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luke Taylor" href="/user/show/30710594-luke-taylor">Luke Taylor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1469185989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12970969622163374610">Cruel Crown is a one stop in the Starbucks with the grande of your choice and a corner table sort of excurison, splitting the difference between two short stories and a tidbit of the yet to be released Glass Sword. I really enjoyed Queen Song, featuring a different style of prose than the traditional broad-brush and salty spunk of Mare Barrow’s plight as the little lightning girl, and seeing into the humanity of Silver politics and personalities was a wise move on Victoria's behalf. Even though </span>
  <span id="freeText12970969622163374610" style="display:none">Cruel Crown is a one stop in the Starbucks with the grande of your choice and a corner table sort of excurison, splitting the difference between two short stories and a tidbit of the yet to be released Glass Sword. I really enjoyed Queen Song, featuring a different style of prose than the traditional broad-brush and salty spunk of Mare Barrow’s plight as the little lightning girl, and seeing into the humanity of Silver politics and personalities was a wise move on Victoria's behalf. Even though anyone can betray anyone, Queen Song gives more food for thought in the way of good and evil, right and wrong, rather than Red vs Silver. So, in the books to come, hopefully one would not think all Silvers are inherently bad and all Reds are good. Such is not the case. People are people, no matter what their blood. Steel Scars gives us the other side of the coin, the grit of Norta falling south of heaven, and another version of resistance leader Farley’s destined connection with Little Miss Red in the head, Silver in the heart herself.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452496562ra/17698980.gif" width="300" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So then this is me reading the Glass Sword sneak preview, going, “And the rest is...where?” *Looks at calender* “Umm...”<br><br>So that’s the “Cruel” portion of the book, I guess…<br><br>Beautiful stuff again from Victoria, as always. :D</span>
  <a data-text-id="12970969622163374610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4481583238879094172">2.5 stars<br/><br/>I quite enjoyed 'Queen Song' and would have loved to read more of that storyline. 'Steel Scars' on the other hand, I could have cared less about. I'm not a fan of Captian Farley and found myself skimming through this one just to get it over with. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1555824176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1555824176" />
    <a title="Donita Luz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18877120-donita-luz"><img alt="Donita Luz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447515803p2/18877120.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1555824176?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donita Luz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donita Luz" href="/user/show/18877120-donita-luz">Donita Luz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18877120-donita-luz?shelf=novellas">novellas</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1555824176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5337189069818511998"><blockquote>
  <i>"He was the prince. the future king. And she was no one at all, a limp excuse for a Silver daughter of a High House."</i>
</blockquote> This novella was clever. I have been so curious with the story of the first queen, Cal's mother story. All we got to know her was that she was Julian's sister, a Singer, and the queen before the cold-hearted Elara took over. It was written on a third-person point of view given the fact that Queen Coriane has already past away - I wasn't expecting that. I thought that this nov</span>
  <span id="freeText5337189069818511998" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"He was the prince. the future king. And she was no one at all, a limp excuse for a Silver daughter of a High House."</i>
</blockquote> This novella was clever. I have been so curious with the story of the first queen, Cal's mother story. All we got to know her was that she was Julian's sister, a Singer, and the queen before the cold-hearted Elara took over. It was written on a third-person point of view given the fact that Queen Coriane has already past away - I wasn't expecting that. I thought that this novella was going to be composed of entry on a Diary where the Queen kept all of her secrets - I was obviously wrong and it was the best mistake ever.<br /><br /><b>Queen Song</b> was simply amazing. Coriane and Tibe's love story was also included and even though it was not really detailed I couldn't have asked for more. It was like a Cinderella story, only Coriane was not a slave. Although they are poor, they still belong to a High House with a Silver Blood and instead of a wicked Step-mother, we got here instead a wicked/evil Queen wanna-be in Elara. Even though their story was tragic-compare to the happy ending in Cinderella story, it was sweet and believable, being a crowned prince and all. We also get to follow the Queen's happiness and hurt and anger and desperation and depression when she was finally able to get a son, Cal, after the 3rd miscarriage. <br /><br />Her characterization was well portrayed, although a bit unlikeable. She likes to down herself a lot even before she met the crowned prince. She was always moping around feeling sorry for herself and for the dream she wouldn't be able to live. She was weak. She did tried to fight, however, she didn't know her enemy well which eventually end up to her death as we all know.<br /><br />The ending was obviously rushed. I think it has something to do with the secrecy and mystery that the book is trying to keep up. Although we all have our suspicions, the question still remains on who really is behind the Queen's death? And if our suspicions was right.. How?<blockquote>
  <i>"We succeed where others can't. We survive. Now I must do the same alone. Now I have to protect others, taking their lives-and deaths-onto my shoulders."</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Steel Cars</b>, on the other hand was so boooring I find myself dozing of a lot of times. It actually took me 3 days to finish reading this, a real feat, considering it was just a novella with more or less a 100 pages.<br /><br />This Novella was from Farley's, The Scarlet Guard Captain's POV. I was really surprised since her character here was so different from the Farley I imagined on The Red Queen. She was only 22 years old and hungry to prove her worth to her commander, I totally thought she was a older than that. She was vulnerable here totally different from the Farley in the first book that I met. Reading her POV was all sorts of boring. There weren't any real action that you would have expect from the leader of a rebellion! This short novella also left me confused as hell.<br /><br />I find it funny how Farley and all of her people can infiltrate and walk around the Stilts easily like they are from Norta. I mean, I remember Mare noting Farley as a Foreigner, a Lakelander, at first sight, so how can they walk around the Norta lands without raising any suspicions at all? I thought they were in war with the Lakelanders for the lands- the point of conscription in the first place right? That was the first war before the Scarlet Guard rage their own war against the Silver? For equality?<br /><br />Then there's all those decoded message from the Scarlet Guard. I won't even pretend to understand them because I didn't and I still don't. I didn't even bother remembering all their code names when they are using their real names all the time. <br /><br />Obviously, I have way too many issue with this novella to enjoy it. The only reason why it's gotten a 2 star rating from me was because of <b>Shade Barrow</b>. Yes, Mare Barrow charismatic brother and because of Farley and Shade's hinted romance in there that I've never really notice after reading 11 chapters from the Glass Sword <b>(Yes, I've read 11 chapters from the Glass Sword before I decided to read this novella firs. Don't judge me. lol)</b>. Remind me again why this novella wasn't about Shade or Maven instead? Oh yeah well, maybe for Girl Power? :|<br /><br />Queen Song - 4 Stars<br />Steel Cars - 2 Stars<br /><br />Want more reviews? :) <br /><br />Check out my friend Pearly's wonderful and detailed review <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1364103648?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> It's amazing how we have almost the same reaction with this novella! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5337189069818511998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2895863615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4474738552467218915"><b>***I reviewed both books individually.***</b><br/><br/><b>Book One:</b> Oueen Song - ★★★★★'s<br/><br/><b>Heart Breaking</b> <br/><br/>“She was happy, yes, in her own way, as best as she knew.<br/>But there’s a difference between a single candle in darkness and a sunrise.”<br/><br/>Oh my goodness, this was so darn sad! From beginning to end I felt my heart getting heavier and heavier with heartache for Coriane. That poor girl, she was so sweet and had such a gentle soul. She didn't deserve all the shit she had to suffer through. Elara as we already knew was </span>
  <span id="freeText4474738552467218915" style="display:none"><b>***I reviewed both books individually.***</b><br><br><b>Book One:</b> Oueen Song - ★★★★★'s<br><br><b>Heart Breaking</b> <br><br>“She was happy, yes, in her own way, as best as she knew.<br>But there’s a difference between a single candle in darkness and a sunrise.”<br><br>Oh my goodness, this was so darn sad! From beginning to end I felt my heart getting heavier and heavier with heartache for Coriane. That poor girl, she was so sweet and had such a gentle soul. She didn't deserve all the shit she had to suffer through. Elara as we already knew was an evil corrupted bitch but this really shows just how black her heart and her soul really was, all to win a Crown!!! It was also nice getting to see that Prince Tibe chose Coriane because he truly unwaveringly loved her, Queenstrial be damned! It also gives us a better understanding as to why he favored Cal so much. Because Cal was all he had felt of the Women he loved. Coriane had so much love for baby Cal. Cal was her light on her darkest of days. Ugh just writing this is making me sad all over again 😭. I love the way this was written, it really drew me in and I couldn't read it fast enough. Hell, I wish it was a LOT longer. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531005502ra/25939766.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Book Two:</b> Steel Scars - ★★'s<br><br><b>Red as the dawn</b><br><br>“Will you oath yourself to the Scarlet Guard?” <br>“On one condition.” <br>“The Guard does not bargain.” <br>“This isn't a request to the Guard, but to you.” <br>“And that is?” <br>"What's your name?” <br>“My name is Diana... <br>Are you with us, Shade Barrow?"<br>“I'm with you, Diana.” <br>“Then we will rise.” <br>“Red as the dawn.” <br><br>Novellas have never been my thing but I was really hoping this would be as good as Queen Song (o.1) but it wasn't. Anyways, that being said this is from Farleys POV. I was never truly invested in her character/story nor was she ever a favorite character of mine but... it was kinda cool being able to see some earlier operations that lead up to Red Queen. I loved getting to seeing how Farley and Shade met. I've always loved Shade and I wish Victoria Aveyard would have pushed that further. For the most part, I found it to be repetitive and boring. Wish this was Shades POV instead.</span>

  <span id="freeText11295307813988555088" style="display:none"><b>QUEEN SONG</b><br /><br />Basically, Queen Song is about a depressed, sad girl with a diary. She thought herself as nothing. <div id="review_1362253595" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1362253595" />
    <a title="Meghan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20870487-meghan"><img alt="Meghan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435602537p2/20870487.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1362253595?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meghan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meghan" href="/user/show/20870487-meghan">Meghan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20870487-meghan?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20870487-meghan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20870487-meghan?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1362253595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18424798848603429493">Okay, so this was the surprise of my year so far. I have read both Red Queen and Glass Sword and to say that I didn't love them is an understatement. I thought they were okay but not amazing. Imagine my surprise when I picked up Cruel Crown this evening and ended up giving it five stars! These two short stories were amazing! They made me want to pick up Kings Cage right away, which is impressive because I have been holding off on reading that one since I bought it. These two stories were so char</span>
  <span id="freeText18424798848603429493" style="display:none">Okay, so this was the surprise of my year so far. I have read both Red Queen and Glass Sword and to say that I didn't love them is an understatement. I thought they were okay but not amazing. Imagine my surprise when I picked up Cruel Crown this evening and ended up giving it five stars! These two short stories were amazing! They made me want to pick up Kings Cage right away, which is impressive because I have been holding off on reading that one since I bought it. These two stories were so character specific and beautiful! I loved them both so much! Aveyard changed my opinion about her in less than 200 pages and I'm not even sorry! <br /><br />Longer review coming soon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18424798848603429493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11277069992569635994">I wasn't a big fan of <i>Red Queen</i> to be honest; I'm not saying that it was a bad book, I just found it rather boring myself. However, one thing I love about books is that if you dislike the first book in the series, you can still have faith in its prequel or sequel. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454219388ra/17931892.gif' width='500' height='248' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Cruel Crown</i> was so much better than I was expecting, and I'm glad that I decided to give the series a second chance because it was totally worthwhile to find out some of the past story behind <i>Red Queen</i>, in fact it kind of filled in any</span>
  <span id="freeText11277069992569635994" style="display:none">I wasn't a big fan of <i>Red Queen</i> to be honest; I'm not saying that it was a bad book, I just found it rather boring myself. Now I really want to read the second book in the series, apparently it's coming out this year. :)</span>

<div id="review_1520256089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1520256089" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5222160-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525911009p2/5222160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1520256089?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/5222160-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1520256089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15194957883208263988"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25944381.Cruel_Crown__Red_Queen___0_1__0_2_' title='Cruel Crown (Red Queen, #0.1-#0.2) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cruel Crown</a> consists of two novellas, Queen Song and Steel Scars, that are prequels to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_' title='Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red Queen</a>. I wanted to read these prequels before starting <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23174274.Glass_Sword__Red_Queen___2_' title='Glass Sword (Red Queen, #2) by Victoria Aveyard' rel='nofollow noopener'>Glass Sword</a> in case there was any information in them that would make me feel lost in the second book of the series.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>Queen Song</b>
</i> ☆☆☆<br/>I read this first prequel nearly a month ago before putting the book aside to read other things. I was a little all over the the place this month and started a lot of books all near the same time that I'm just now wrappi</span>
  <span id="freeText15194957883208263988" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25944381.Cruel_Crown__Red_Queen___0_1__0_2_" title="Cruel Crown (Red Queen, #0.1-#0.2) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Crown</a> consists of two novellas, Queen Song and Steel Scars, that are prequels to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>. I wanted to read these prequels before starting <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23174274.Glass_Sword__Red_Queen___2_" title="Glass Sword (Red Queen, #2) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Glass Sword</a> in case there was any information in them that would make me feel lost in the second book of the series.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Queen Song</b>
</i> ☆☆☆<br />I read this first prequel nearly a month ago before putting the book aside to read other things. I was a little all over the the place this month and started a lot of books all near the same time that I'm just now wrapping up. I don't remember a lot of specific details of this book except that it is the story of how Coriane, Cal's mother, became queen without having to win Queenstrial. Her family had lost the majority of their fortune and with Queenstrial looming in the near future, she didn't believe she had any chance of winning the crown since she had nothing to offer. True love wins in the end, though - sort of.<br /><br />Although I know there have been many kings in real history who have taken lovers openly, it really seemed odd how casual everyone was with King Tiberias V's lover. His marriage to Anabel was for nothing more than producing an heir. I felt sorry for her. Would it have been as acceptable for her to take a lover openly as well? Overall, I didn't enjoy this prequel as much as many others. It was nice learning about how Coriane and Tiberias VI met and fell in love, but it didn't shed a whole lot of extra light on what had already been revealed in Red Queen.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Steel Scars</b>
</i> ☆☆☆☆☆<br />I'm in the minority with this prequel as well, because from most of the reviews I've read, people didn't like this one. I loved it! We knew close to nothing about Farley from Red Queen, and this prequel gave us a glimpse of who she was before the Scarlet Guard's attack on Norta. We got to know her as a person and as a revolutionist. <br /><br />I don't want to give too much away - So, I'll try to keep the synopsis brief and a bit vague. Diana Farley grew up and lived most of her life in the Lakelands. She joined the Scarlet Guard because she hated what the Silvers were doing to her people and eventually climbed the ranks to become a captain. Farley crossed the border to Norta for the first time only a few weeks before the bombings. With the setup of the Scarlet Guard, she didn't know what the main mission was because individuals are only given enough information for them to complete their assignments. I really hope I see more of Farley in Glass Sword. I really like her character, and I hope she succeeds. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15194957883208263988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Alice (Married To Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45911840-alice-married-to-books"><img alt="Alice (Married To Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447366818p2/45911840.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1690697570?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alice (Married To Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alice (Married To Books)" href="/user/show/45911840-alice-married-to-books">Alice (Married To Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1690697570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13913354781070700211">I won a copy of Cruel Crown via a Twitter giveaway! Disclaimer: I have NOT read the extract of Glass Sword as I would rather read/review it once I get a copy of the novel in full!<br/><br/>I'm feeling extremely conflicted about how to review this novella bide-up. Queen Song was a quick read with a good plot. It was nice to return to the Red Queen world and enjoyed following Coriane receive a diary in which she writes about her honest thoughts towards her family and relationship to the heir Prince Tiberias</span>
  <span id="freeText13913354781070700211" style="display:none">I won a copy of Cruel Crown via a Twitter giveaway! Disclaimer: I have NOT read the extract of Glass Sword as I would rather read/review it once I get a copy of the novel in full!<br /><br />I'm feeling extremely conflicted about how to review this novella bide-up. Queen Song was a quick read with a good plot. It was nice to return to the Red Queen world and enjoyed following Coriane receive a diary in which she writes about her honest thoughts towards her family and relationship to the heir Prince Tiberias. I always like it when a story is either written in diary form or one of the main characters receives a diary to write in. <br /><br />Steel Scars scores an 11/10 for world-building and thrills, it was longer to read than Queen Song but after reading a few action-packed books recently, I loved experiencing the thrills. This novella is told in Farley's POV which I was rather surprised about but also felt quite refreshing as I was interested in Farley's character after reading Red Queen.<br /><br />I would recommend reading these novellas after Red Queen but before Glass Sword. It was nice to return to the world that Victoria Aveyard has written about, if there's one book that you should read this year, it's Red Queen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13913354781070700211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2725454231" />
    <a title="Jenn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn"><img alt="Jenn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360078699p2/3957464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2725454231?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn" href="/user/show/3957464-jenn">Jenn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28465789-cruel-crown">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=do-you-believe-in-magic">do-you-believe-in-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=3-star-reads">3-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3957464-jenn?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2725454231" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2003444120314187904"><b>2.5 but rounding up for <i>Queen Song</i></b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Queen Song</u>
</b><br/>This was definitely the better of the two novellas but I felt it needed to be a little bit longer because we were never able to really dive into Coriane and the horrible fate that took her away. There was a lot of time setting up her life before court which wasn't that interesting and probably could have been told in less time to be able to add more to her time at court and with the future king. I did enjoy her POV and I felt really bad for her. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText2003444120314187904" style="display:none"><b>2.5 but rounding up for <i>Queen Song</i></b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Queen Song</u>
</b><br />This was definitely the better of the two novellas but I felt it needed to be a little bit longer because we were never able to really dive into Coriane and the horrible fate that took her away. There was a lot of time setting up her life before court which wasn't that interesting and probably could have been told in less time to be able to add more to her time at court and with the future king. I did enjoy her POV and I felt really bad for her. The relationship between her and the king was sweet and I believed their connection was real. It's crazy to see just how far Elara went to procure the crown. And also, you think that the Silvers would have some way to protect themselves from Whispers. I mean, they're supposed to be the "superior" race and they couldn't think of a way to block a Whisperer from taking over their mind?<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Steel Scars<u></u></u>
</b><br />Sadly, this one was just boring. What was supposed to be a glimpse into Farleys meeting with Shade and the beginning of their relationship was more like Farley trying to impress her dad for over 100 pages. The only parts I liked were Shade's introduction and when he revealed his power to Farley. Everything else was a mess and just boring. And this was $2.99 on Amazon? A giant waste of money.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2003444120314187904" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1680858086" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14113776001141420945">6/VI/18 Reread:<br/>I don't have much to say about this. It was okay. I think my previous review says all that can be said about this book. I wouldn't mind if Farley's story had been expanded. She's one of my favorite characters. Coriane's story was still kinda pointless, but at least it's super short. <br/><br/>____________________________________________________________<br/>The Backstory of Red Queen: The First Betrayal & the Start of the Scarlet Guard<br/>Cruel Crown<br/>Overall Rating: 3/5<br/>Queen’s Song: 2/5<br/><br/>This is the sto</span>
  <span id="freeText14113776001141420945" style="display:none">6/VI/18 Reread:<br />I don't have much to say about this. It was okay. I think my previous review says all that can be said about this book. I wouldn't mind if Farley's story had been expanded. She's one of my favorite characters. Coriane's story was still kinda pointless, but at least it's super short. <br /><br />____________________________________________________________<br />The Backstory of Red Queen: The First Betrayal &amp; the Start of the Scarlet Guard<br />Cruel Crown<br />Overall Rating: 3/5<br />Queen’s Song: 2/5<br /><br />This is the story of Coriane Jacos, the mother of Cal from Red Queen. Coriane is nothing special and her house is falling on hard times. Her uncle that governors the House is old and dying; while her father has ambition, he is a terrible leader. When Coriane befriends Tiberias the Sixth, aka the Crown Prince, her father believes he has found the answer to all his problems, while Coriane believes she has found a friend as lonely as her. <br /><br />The story was cute, but I didn’t really feel any attraction from Coriane to Tibe. It seemed like he was desperately holding on to her and she went with it because she had no other options. She doesn’t like court life and all she wants to do is be a mechanic or builder. She resents the way her world treats Reds and Silvers, but has no way to do anything about it. Even as Queen she does not try. However, her mind is assaulted by Elara, the evil bitch that will birth Maven. The way she tampered felt very subtle and I wasn’t sure if it actually happened, I would have liked it to be a little clearer. I enjoyed it, but it felt too short to be substantial. <br />*I loved seeing Julian and Sarah together just being happy. Julian is one of my favorite characters.<br /><br />Steel Scars<br />Rating: 4/5<br /><br />The Scarlet Guard began somewhere and Farley had a lot to do with it. After years of working with her Father- the Colonel- it’s time for Farley to strike out on her own as a Captain. We learn more about the Guard and Farley’s involvement, as well as a little bit from the mysterious Command. Farley’s mission is to begin to make contact and allies in Norta so that the Guard can Rise, Red as the Dawn.<br /><br />I enjoyed this one more, because it was longer and easier to get in to. Farley has spunk and passion, whereas Coriane felt kind of pale and dull in comparison. Also, I really enjoyed the way the guard sent coded messages, it was quite brilliant. Another reason I liked this story is SHADE. I LOVE HIM!!! I NEED MORE OF SHADE &amp; FARLEY. Besides that, this story had more action and the danger was always lingering overhead. I would recommend these since it’s a quick read and gives nice backstory to the Red Queen universe.</span>

    <a title="Acqua" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47160872-acqua"><img alt="Acqua" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548417878p2/47160872.jpg" /></a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=love-cover">love-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47160872-acqua?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1492770330" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3123749947326572927">This is a bind-up of the two <i>Red Queen</i> novellas, <i>Cruel Crown</i> and <i>Steel Scars</i>.<br/><br/><b>I loved <i>Queen Song</i>. It's better than every book I've read so far by this author</b>, and I think Aveyard writes better in third person PoV. It was really interesting to see the silvers from the inside, and Queen Coriane's story was heartbreaking. In this world, the reds suffer because they're poor and they do not have powers, but life as a silver is not easy. Coriane would like to change things, but as this story shows, the</span>
  <span id="freeText3123749947326572927" style="display:none">This is a bind-up of the two <i>Red Queen</i> novellas, <i>Cruel Crown</i> and <i>Steel Scars</i>.<br /><br /><b>I loved <i>Queen Song</i>. It's better than every book I've read so far by this author</b>, and I think Aveyard writes better in third person PoV. It was really interesting to see the silvers from the inside, and Queen Coriane's story was heartbreaking. In this world, the reds suffer because they're poor and they do not have powers, but life as a silver is not easy. Coriane would like to change things, but as this story shows, the other silvers do not have the same ideas.<br />It made me cry, and I rated it 5 stars.<br /><br /><i>Steel Scars</i>, however, was kind of boring at times. Yes, I got to know Farley's story (and her PoV) and that was great, but it was too long and repetitive at times; <b>it had none of the emotional impact <i>Queen Song</i> had</b>. I rated it 3.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3123749947326572927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('M/TW9qXN8s6hHxPZvyWXt5/CTRsgpgC2m5HDtCyfT21i4EDNFQ9lj3aPx8qWes996WC3j6pJJ6NdrPoLPTE0HQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('R3jWVGToTNTelmWLVUnBC38gpD/D/qFFLSmS2/hajx0WbEBv1CrblQkGsZh8FpnBCYJeq0kRhlDrFKtk6fT0bQ==')})
  }
